### 🤖 Assistant

Here's what's being built across the live sessions.

## The big picture: real-time agent-to-agent comms on Panopticon

There's one major active planning+build session (`89df0e0b`, started ~18:07, the `/plan` session running on Opus 4.8) that spawned a fleet of subagents to scope a Claude Code **build/demo day project**. The full plan lives at `~/.claude/plans/lets-discuss-a-project-temporal-sparkle.md`.

**The core idea:** Today two concurrent Panopticon sessions can only *passively* observe each other through the shared DB. This project adds a **real-time agent-to-agent comms bus** brokered by the existing Panopticon server (`:4318`), then lands the headline feature on top:

- **Frenemy** — a *real second agent session* (model/vendor configurable) launched via `panopticon frenemy` that runs alongside your primary agent in the same workspace, watches its moves over the bus, and posts **adversarial challenges**. The primary hears them via Panopticon's existing `additionalContext` hook injection at its next tool/prompt round-trip. Demo: primary tries to delete a flaky test → frenemy challenges it → primary reconsiders, live.
- **Sidequest** — parallel agents in separate worktrees coordinating non-colliding edits into separate PRs. Explicitly a **stretch goal**; the v1 primitives are shaped so it's additive (claims projection over the same message log).

## Architecture (4 incremental PRs, one per layer)

- **Layer 0 — instance presence + reaper** ← *being built right now, this branch*
- **Layer 1 — the bus primitive** (`agent_messages` table, `bus_send`/`bus_read`/`bus_roster` MCP tools, implicit workspace-superset rooms)
- **Layer 2 — hook publish/drain + fs-watch** (⚠️ flagged provisional — the eventual-delivery / PreToolUse-drain design wasn't fully convincing yet)
- **Layer 3 — frenemy agent** on the `/panopticon` skill+command surface

Key design decisions already locked: **rooms are implicit & workspace-scoped** (derived from repo, no tokens to type); **liveness via active PID probing, not heartbeat decay** (a heartbeat can't tell "idle/thinking" from "killed").

## Current state on your branch (`layer0-instance-presence`)

You're checked out on the Layer 0 work-in-progress — this matches the active session's edits exactly:

- **New:** `src/presence/store.ts` (instance upsert/query) and `src/presence/reaper.ts` (PID-probe liveness loop) — both untracked
- **Modified:** `src/db/schema.ts` (+27, the `panopticon_instances` table), `src/hooks/handler.ts` (+8, forwards agent PID via `process.ppid`), `src/hooks/ingest.ts` (heartbeat upsert), `src/server.ts` (+8, wires the reaper into bootstrap), `src/log.ts`

Nothing committed yet — Layer 0 is mid-flight. The plan calls for the reaper to mark instances `exited (pid_dead)` on `process.kill(pid, 0)` → `ESRCH`, which is what catches kills/crashes/closed terminals that never fire a clean `SessionEnd`.

Want me to dig into the actual Layer 0 implementation to check it against the plan, or look at any specific layer in more detail?

### 🤖 Assistant

This is the visual payoff of the whole Frenemy/bus project — being able to *watch* the frenemy challenge the primary live. Here's where things stand and my thinking.

## What exists vs. what's needed

**Ready to build on:**
- Unified server on `:4318` (raw Node `http`), authenticated `/api/tool` dispatch
- The data is all there: `panopticon_instances` (presence/roster with `active`/`idle`/`exited` status) from your Layer 0 work, and `agent_messages` (the bus feed) coming in Layer 1
- A reaper already updating liveness every 7s

**Not there yet (the gaps):**
- **No static file serving** — server is JSON-only, zero HTML
- **No client-facing real-time push** — the WS plumbing that exists is *proxy-only* (tunneling to Claude/OpenAI upstreams), not a broadcast bus to browsers. So today a UI would have to poll.
- **Zero frontend deps/tooling** — no React/Vite, just `tsup` for the CLI

## My recommendation (demo-day shaped)

A single **Mission Control** page that shows two things side by side: the **live roster** (who's connected, active/idle/exited) and the **bus feed** (activity + frenemy challenges streaming in). That's the money shot — kill the primary's terminal and watch it flip to `exited`; watch a 🔴 challenge appear the instant the frenemy sends it.

The leanest architecture that fits the existing raw-`http` design and demos well:
- **Add SSE + static serving to the existing `:4318` server** — no separate web server, no Electron. SSE (not WebSocket) because the dashboard is read-only/one-directional, it's plain HTTP, and needs zero deps. Broadcast on instance upsert/reap and on bus-message insert.
- **One vanilla HTML/JS page, no build step** — keeps it consistent with the zero-frontend-deps repo and means nothing to bundle. The server injects the auth token into the page server-side (localhost-only, so fine).

This avoids a framework, a build pipeline, and a second process — all of which are demo-day risk.

A couple of decisions are genuinely yours before I scope it:

### 🤖 Assistant

Got it — **Mission Control now, architected so it can grow into a full app.** That mostly shapes *where the durable seams go*: the server-side contract (static serving + a typed SSE event stream + the existing `/api/tool` dispatch) is the part that has to be stable and framework-agnostic. The frontend itself can start as a no-build vanilla page for the demo and be swapped for a Vite/React build later **without touching the server** — as long as the event contract is right from day one. Let me lay out the concrete design.

## Architecture

### Server side (all under a new `src/ui/`)

**1. A generic broadcaster — `src/ui/events.ts`**
An in-process pub/sub singleton holding the set of connected SSE clients. Typed events so it scales beyond Mission Control:
```ts
type UiEvent =
  | { type: "instance"; data: InstanceRow }   // presence change
  | { type: "message";  data: AgentMessage }  // bus message
  // later: "session" | "cost" | "rebuild" | ...
```
Both presence code and bus code just call `broadcast(event)` — they don't know about HTTP.

**2. SSE endpoint — `GET /api/events`** (wired into `src/server.ts` routing alongside `/api/*`)
Holds the connection open, writes `data: {...}\n\n` per event. EventSource can't send custom headers, so auth rides as a query param (`?token=…`) or cookie — fine on localhost.

**3. Emit points (one-liners into existing code):**
- `upsertInstance` + `reapDeadInstances` (`src/presence/store.ts`, your Layer 0) → `broadcast({type:"instance"})`
- `insertAgentMessage` (`src/db/bus.ts`, Layer 1) → `broadcast({type:"message"})`

**4. Static serving — `GET /ui`** serves one HTML page; the server injects the auth token into the page at serve time (localhost-only). Serve from a configurable dir so a future `web/dist` build can drop in.

### Client side — `src/ui/web/` (vanilla, no build)
One `index.html` + `app.js` + `style.css`. On load: fetch initial state via existing tools (`instances` / `bus_roster` + `bus_read`), then open `EventSource('/api/events')` for deltas. Two panels:
- **Roster** — instances with status dots (🟢 active / 🟡 idle / ⚪ exited), target, branch, frenemy role highlighted
- **Bus feed** — chronological messages; 🔴 challenges styled prominently, activity muted, showing from→to and `ref_path`

## The one sequencing reality

This branch (`layer0-instance-presence`) has **presence (Layer 0) but not the bus (Layer 1)** — `agent_messages` / `src/db/bus.ts` don't exist yet. So:

- The **roster half works against real data today.**
- The **bus-feed half has no data source until Layer 1 lands.** I'd build the full UI now (broadcaster, SSE, both panels) and wire the presence emits live; the bus emit is a single call that Layer 1's `insertAgentMessage` will make once it exists. The feed renders empty-but-ready until then.

That keeps the UI as a clean PR layered on top, consistent with the "one PR per layer" plan (this is effectively the Mission Control stretch item, pulled forward).

**Before I build:** do you want me to (a) build the full Mission Control now on this branch — roster live, bus feed wired-and-waiting — or (b) wait until Layer 1 exists so the whole thing demos end-to-end immediately? I lean (a): the SSE + static + roster is real, testable progress right now, and the feed lights up for free when the bus lands.

### 🧑 User

I know it is probably preferable not to start with some sort of framework but what if we made an electron app

### 🤖 Assistant

Electron is a legitimately good fit for the *ambition* you stated ("fully featured app") — but the important reframe is that **it doesn't change the server work at all, and that's where the real engineering is.**

## The key insight: the server contract is identical either way

The durable, valuable part of the design — the SSE broadcaster, the typed event stream, the emit points in presence/bus — is the same whether the client is a browser tab or an Electron renderer. Electron's renderer *is* Chromium; it consumes `EventSource('/api/events')` and `/api/tool` exactly like a browser. So choosing Electron now wastes none of the server work, and the choice stays **reversible**. That means we should build the server side first regardless, and treat browser-vs-Electron as a client-shell decision we can defer or even do both.

## What Electron genuinely buys *this* app (not just vibes)

There are real, project-specific wins beyond "it's a window":
- **Native OS notifications when a frenemy challenge arrives** — even when the dashboard isn't focused. For an adversarial-collaborator tool, an ambient "🔴 Frenemy challenged your edit" toast is a *killer demo moment* and genuinely useful.
- **Tray icon / always-on-top ambient watcher** — Mission Control as a persistent corner-of-screen presence, not a tab you forget.
- **Direct filesystem access** kills the token-injection hack: the main process just reads `~/.panopticon/auth-token` and the `.pid` file to discover port + auth. Cleaner.
- A real product surface that matches "fully featured app."

## The honest costs

- The repo today has **zero frontend deps** and builds a CLI with `tsup`. Electron + electron-builder is a heavy departure — hundreds of MB, a separate build/packaging pipeline, code signing if you ever distribute.
- Two-process (main/renderer/IPC) complexity.
- **Demo-day risk:** more moving parts than "open localhost in the browser you already have."

## My recommendation

**Build the web app so it runs in both a browser tab and an Electron shell, and isolate Electron in its own package** (e.g. `apps/mission-control/`) so the lean core `panopticon` package never takes on Electron deps. Concretely:

1. **Server side (now, shared):** SSE broadcaster + event contract + static serving — as designed.
2. **Frontend (now, shared):** the Mission Control page. It runs in any Chromium — browser *or* Electron renderer. Same code.
3. **Electron shell (thin, additive):** a small `main.js` that opens a `BrowserWindow` on the served page, reads the token from disk, and adds the native layer (tray + OS notification on `type:"message"` challenge events from the SSE stream). ~100 lines, no impact on core.

This gives you the native-app payoff *and* a zero-risk browser fallback for the demo, with no lock-in and no wasted work. The only real "Electron tax" is the packaging pipeline, and isolating it in its own dir contains the blast radius.

One thing worth deciding, since it affects how I structure the Electron shell:

### 🤖 Assistant

Good news that sharpens the plan: **Layer 0 is essentially complete** — the `instances` tool already exists end-to-end (service `direct.ts:193` + `http.ts:139`, transport `transport.ts:49`, MCP `server.ts:825`, CLI `cli.ts:1829`). So the roster has a live data source **today** via `/api/tool { name: "instances" }`. The bus feed waits on Layer 1, exactly as expected.

Here's the concrete build plan.

## Implementation plan

### Server side — new `src/ui/` (in core package)

**`src/ui/events.ts`** — generic SSE broadcaster
- Module-level `Set<http.ServerResponse>` of connected clients
- `broadcast(event: UiEvent)` writes `data: ${JSON}\n\n` to each; prunes dead sockets
- Typed `UiEvent` union: `{type:"instance",data}` / `{type:"message",data}` — extensible to `session`/`cost`/`rebuild` later
- Zero deps, no coupling to HTTP routing details

**`src/ui/sse.ts`** — `handleEventStream(req,res)`
- Sets SSE headers, registers the response in the broadcaster, sends a `:ping` keepalive on an interval, cleans up on `close`
- Auth via `?token=` query param (EventSource can't set headers); validated against the boot token

**`src/ui/static.ts`** — `handleUiRequest(req,res)`
- Serves `src/ui/web/*` (html/js/css), correct content-types, path-traversal guard
- Injects the auth token + port into `index.html` at serve time so the page can call `/api/tool` and open the SSE stream

**`src/server.ts`** — wire 3 routes before the 404 (mirrors existing `url.startsWith` style):
- `GET /api/events` → `handleEventStream` (the only `/api/` GET; current `/api/` block is POST-only, so no conflict)
- `GET /ui` and `GET /ui/*` → `handleUiRequest`

**Emit points (2 one-liners, both already in code I've read):**
- `src/presence/store.ts` `upsertInstance` + `endInstance` → `broadcast({type:"instance", data: <row+derived status>})`. Plus a hook so the reaper's `onReap` broadcasts exits (wire `onReap` in `server.ts:251` where the reaper is created).
- `src/db/bus.ts` `insertAgentMessage` → `broadcast({type:"message",…})` — added when Layer 1 lands (single line; renders empty-but-ready until then).

### Frontend — `src/ui/web/` (vanilla, no build)
- `index.html` + `app.js` + `style.css`
- On load: seed state from `/api/tool {name:"instances"}` (+ `bus_read` when it exists), then `new EventSource('/api/events?token=…')` for deltas
- **Roster panel:** status dots (🟢 active / 🟡 idle / ⚪ exited), target, branch, role (frenemy highlighted)
- **Bus feed panel:** chronological; 🔴 challenges prominent, activity muted, from→to + `ref_path`

### Electron shell — `apps/mission-control/` (isolated package, zero core impact)
- `package.json` (electron + electron-builder as devDeps, **not** in core)
- `main.js`: discovers data dir (replicates `resolveDataDir`), reads token from `<dataDir>/auth-token`, finds port via `<dataDir>/panopticon.pid` / `/health`; opens a `BrowserWindow` on `http://127.0.0.1:<port>/ui`
- Native layer: tray icon; **OS notification on SSE `type:"message"` challenge events** (main process holds its own EventSource-equivalent, or the renderer forwards via IPC)
- The same web page runs unchanged in a browser → zero-risk demo fallback

### Verification
- `pnpm check && pnpm typecheck && pnpm test`; unit-test the broadcaster (subscribe/broadcast/prune) and SSE auth
- Manual: start server, open `/ui` in a browser, launch a second `claude` session → watch it appear in the roster; kill it → watch it flip to `exited` within a reaper interval. Then `electron .` for the native window + a test notification.

**Sequencing:** everything except the one `bus.ts` emit line and the feed's data binding works against today's Layer 0. I'd build it all now; the feed lights up automatically when Layer 1 lands.

Want me to start building, or adjust the plan first? If you're good, I'll begin with the server-side `src/ui/` (broadcaster + SSE + static + route wiring + presence emits) since that's the durable foundation, then the frontend, then the Electron shell.

### 🤖 Assistant

This is the right thing to check first, and the answer changes the plan. Here's the real picture:

## The actual risk isn't file overlap — it's a shared working tree

`git worktree list` shows **one** checkout: `/Users/gus/workspace/panopticon` on `layer0-instance-presence`. The other major session (`89df0e0b`) has the **same `cwd`** — so right now we'd both be editing one directory and one git index. And it's live: Layer 0 just got **committed 4 minutes ago** (the previously-uncommitted presence files are gone from `git status`), which means that session is actively running git here and is about to start Layer 1.

Two agents editing the same checkout simultaneously is unsafe regardless of *which* files — their writes interleave, and either side running `git checkout`/`commit`/`stash` yanks files out from under the other. That's the blocker, not the diff.

## Logical file overlap (small, and mostly avoidable)

If we *were* on the same branch, here's the actual contention:

| File | Other session | My UI work | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|
| `src/ui/**`, `apps/mission-control/**` | — | new files | **none** |
| `src/presence/store.ts` | owns (Layer 0, done) | +2 broadcast lines | low |
| `src/server.ts` | adds fs-watch bootstrap (Layer 2) | adds UI routes + reaper `onReap` | **medium** — only genuine co-edit, both in bootstrap region |
| `src/db/bus.ts` | **creates** (Layer 1) | +1 emit line | sequencing, not conflict — they make the file, I add later |

So the only real shared edit is `src/server.ts`, and even that is different regions (route table + reaper wiring vs. the fs-watch handle). Everything else of mine is new files. The bus feed depends on Layer 1 existing, but the **roster works against Layer 0, which is already committed** — so the UI is unblocked.

## Recommendation: isolate in a separate worktree

Yes, we can safely work in parallel — but in our **own git worktree**, not this shared checkout:

```
git worktree add ../panopticon-mission-control -b mission-control-ui
```

This gives us an isolated directory + branch, forked off the current state (which **includes** the committed Layer 0), so:
- Zero working-tree/index collision with the live session.
- The roster half builds immediately (Layer 0 is in our base).
- When Layer 1 lands (on its branch or `main`), I merge it in and add the one `bus.ts` emit line + wire the feed — a clean, deliberate integration rather than a live race.
- The `src/server.ts` overlap resolves as a normal small merge later, not a real-time clobber.

Want me to set up that worktree and start building the UI there? That keeps both efforts fully parallel and safe.

### 🤖 Assistant

Mission Control is built, verified, and isolated from the parallel bus session. Here's where it landed.

## What's built (worktree `../panopticon-mission-control`, branch `mission-control-ui`)

**Server side (`src/ui/`, in core)**
- `events.ts` — generic SSE broadcaster with a typed `UiEvent` union (`instance` | `message`, extensible to sessions/costs/rebuild later)
- `sse.ts` — `GET /api/events`, timing-safe `?token=` auth, keepalive pings
- `static.ts` — `GET /ui`, serves the web app and injects token+port into the HTML shell; path-traversal guarded
- Wired 2 routes + imports into `server.ts`; broadcast emits added to `upsertInstance`/`endInstance` in `presence/store.ts` (guarded by `hasClients()` so the hook hot path stays free — and reaper exits broadcast for free since they go through `endInstance`)
- Build: `scripts/copy-ui-assets.mjs` copies `src/ui/web` → `dist/ui/web` (tsup wipes dist)

**Frontend (`src/ui/web/`, vanilla, no build)** — dark Mission Control page: roster panel (status dots, target, branch, frenemy badge) + bus feed (challenges styled red, activity muted). Seeds from `/api/tool`, live-updates via `EventSource`. Runs in browser *or* Electron unchanged.

**Electron shell (`apps/mission-control/`, isolated package)** — `main.js` discovers the port, waits for `/health`, opens a window on `/ui`, adds a menu-bar tray, and raises native OS notifications on frenemy challenges (renderer → `preload.js` → main IPC). Electron deps kept out of core.

## Verification (all green)
- `pnpm check` (239 files), `pnpm typecheck`, tests — all pass; 4 new broadcaster unit tests
- **Live smoke test** on an isolated port/data-dir: `/health`, `instances` tool, `/ui` token injection, CSS content-type, SSE 401-on-bad-token / `: connected`-on-good, traversal blocked — and the key proof: a hook-driven presence upsert **pushed an `event: instance` frame to the SSE stream in real time**

## Conflict status with the bus session
Zero collision — separate worktree, separate index. The only logical co-edit (`src/server.ts`) is a different region than their Layer 2 fs-watch bootstrap; it'll be a trivial merge. The bus feed is wired-and-waiting: it lights up the moment Layer 1's `insertAgentMessage` calls `broadcast({type:"message"})` — one line.

## Open items / your call
- **Electron not smoke-tested** — `electron` isn't installed (kept out of core). Run `cd apps/mission-control && pnpm install && pnpm start` when you want to see the native window. The web app itself is fully verified in-browser.
- **Not committed** — I held off since you didn't ask. Want me to commit on `mission-control-ui`? (I'll add explicit paths only — the `node_modules` symlink stays out.)
- Tray uses a text glyph (`◎`) rather than a shipped icon binary to avoid committing an asset; easy to swap for a real icon later.

Want me to commit, wire up a real tray icon, or pull in Layer 1 once it lands to demo the feed end-to-end?

## Try it — browser (ready now)

```
http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui
```

You'll see the roster populate live. To watch it react in real time:
- **New session:** open another `claude` in any repo → it appears within a second.
- **Kill detection:** `kill -9` a session's PID (or just close its terminal) → it flips to `exited (pid_dead)` within ~7s (the reaper interval). Contrast with an idle-but-alive session, which shows `idle`, not `exited`.

## Refresh and try it

Reload **http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui** and click any roster row.

A detail drawer slides in from the right with:
- **Header** — target, role (frenemy badge), live status chip (stays in sync via SSE), model, branch, room, full session id
- **Stat tiles** — messages · tool calls · subagents · time span · output tokens
- **Tool usage bar chart** — calls per tool (`Edit`, `Bash`, `Read`, `Agent`…), sorted, scaled
- **Subagents** — each child agent with its model + first prompt
- **Activity timeline** — newest-first vertical timeline of prompts (blue) and tool calls (amber) with file/command hints and durations

Click the `89df0e0b` (bus) session for the richest view — 250 messages, 127 tool calls, 14 subagents.

Interactions: click a row to open · `Esc` or click the backdrop or ✕ to close · the selected row stays highlighted · clicking another row swaps the drawer (with a race guard so a slow fetch can't overwrite a newer selection).

## How it's wired
- Pure additive client work in `src/ui/web/` (`app.js` drawer module + `index.html` markup + `style.css`) — **no server changes**; it just calls the existing `timeline` tool via `/api/tool`.
- Rebuilt → reinstalled global `panopticon` → restarted server (PID 6932, port 4319). `pnpm check` clean across 239 files.

A note on the dev loop: since the server serves assets from the *installed* global build, each web change needs rebuild→reinstall→restart (what I just did). If we're going to iterate fast on the UI, I'd suggest running the server straight from the worktree (`node dist/server.js`) so a change is just `pnpm build` + restart — no reinstall. Want me to switch to that loop?

Next ideas: make the bus feed clickable through to the same drawer, add a cost tile (via the `costs` tool), or live-append new activity to an open drawer. What do you want to rip into next?

Done. Reload **http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui** — the roster rows are now much more insightful.

## What each row now shows

Instead of `claude · branch · id`, each row leads with the session's **title/intent** (the LLM/first-prompt title), then a meta line:

```
🟢 look at the other live sessions to catch up on…
   opus 4.8 · layer1-bus-primitive · 229 msg · $26.43 · 2m        active
```

- **Title** — `sessionSummary.title` (falls back to first prompt, then id), clamped to 2 lines
- **Meta line** — model (`opus 4.8`), branch, message count, cost, and age since last activity — only the parts that exist
- Presence status dot + status label stay as before; clicking still opens the detail drawer

## How it works
- Pure client-side join: roster keeps the `instances` (presence/liveness) and now also pulls the `sessions` tool into a `sessionMeta` map, keyed by session id. Re-fetched every 15s so cost/message counts catch up for in-flight sessions. No server changes.

## The one honest caveat
That exact terminal-tab string — *"Review other live sessions for context"* — is **Claude Code's own generated tab title**, set via terminal escape codes, which panopticon doesn't capture. What you see here is panopticon's session title/intent, which for active sessions is the first prompt ("look at the other live sessions…") rather than Claude's polished summary. They're close but not identical.

If you specifically want Claude's polished one-liner, the path would be capturing it from the session JSONL `summary` records during the scan — a small server-side change. Want me to look into wiring that up, or is the title/model/cost enrichment enough?

### 🤖 Assistant

Done — reload **http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui**.

**Dollars on the list:** each row now has a dedicated right-column cost in green mono (`$30.42`), above the status label — prominent, not buried in the meta line.

**Stops moving so much** — two fixes:
- **Debounced rendering:** presence events from all sessions now coalesce into one re-render every ~700ms instead of re-rendering on every single hook. (Selection clicks and the drawer's live status chip stay instant — only the list bulk-render is debounced.)
- **Stable sort:** rows are ordered by status (active → idle → exited) then by first-seen, so a row keeps its position instead of jumping to the top every time its heartbeat ticks. That reordering was the real source of the churn.

If 700ms feels too laggy or still too jumpy, that one number is easy to dial.

### 🤖 Assistant

Fixed. Reload **http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui** and open a busy session's drawer.

## The bug
The drawer's count tiles were derived from the fetched `timeline`, which I'd capped at `limit: 250`. So `messages` was `min(actual, 250)` — anything bigger pinned at 250. Tool calls and output tokens were similarly windowed.

## The fix
The count tiles now use the **authoritative aggregate** from the `sessions` tool (`messageCount`, `totalOutputTokens`, `totalCost`) — same source the roster uses, no cap. The fetched timeline is now only used for the activity list and tool bars (and bumped to a 500-message window).

New drawer stats (now 6 tiles): **messages · tool calls · subagents · out tok · cost · span**. When the session is bigger than the loaded window, the window-derived ones are honestly labeled — `tool calls (recent)` with a `+`, and `span (recent)` — so they never masquerade as totals.

So the big `/plan` session that was stuck at 250 will now show its real ~500+ message count and its true cost.

## The four features (all live + verified)
- **Mission header** — fleet aggregate strip: active count · $/hr burn · tokens/min · total spend (rates from session-cost deltas between polls).
- **Fleet topology** — roster grouped under room/repo headers with `active/total` counts, and a `⊕N` subagent badge per row (the drawer already lists the subagents).
- **Bus feed (live)** — `insertAgentMessage` now broadcasts every message over SSE; the feed seeds recent history via SQL (since `bus_read` is room-scoped). **This is the demo centerpiece now working.**
- **Operator console** — a compose box in the session drawer sends a `chat`/`challenge` to that session via `/api/exec bus-send`. Verified end-to-end: a send inserts the row → SSE pushes it → it appears in the feed instantly.

That's a human playing frenemy through the dashboard — and when the other session's Layer 2 (hook drain) lands, that same challenge will actually reach the target agent's context.

### 🤖 Assistant

### 🧑 User

Issues found (all non-blocking)

  1. Seed-vs-stream race → duplicate feed rows (low). At the bottom, seed() (async, not awaited) and connectStream() (synchronous EventSource) both
  start. A message arriving over SSE before the bus-seed query runs will be rendered live and re-rendered by the seed's LIMIT 50 history —
  applyMessage has no id-based dedup, so you get a duplicate row at the boundary. Similarly the instances snapshot can instances.set over a fresher
  SSE delta (self-heals on next heartbeat). This is the one I'd actually fix: dedup applyMessage by msg.id, or await seed() before connectStream().
  2. Burn-rate metric caveats (low). refreshSessionMeta pulls sessions with limit: 100, so totalSpend/burn/tokens silently cover only the 100 newest
  sessions. Worse for the rate: when a new session enters that window between polls, its full historical cost is attributed to a single 15s interval
  and spikes burnPerHr; a window slide-out drops sumCost (clamped to 0 by the Math.max). Fine for a glanceable dashboard, but worth a comment so
  nobody trusts it as accounting.
  3. toolHint silently empty on large tool inputs (cosmetic). The client calls timeline without fullPayloads, so inputJson is truncated to 500 chars
  server-side. JSON.parse of the truncated string throws and toolHint returns "", so hints just vanish for any tool call with >500-char input. Not a
  crash; consider requesting fullPayloads for the drawer or extracting the hint more defensively.
  4. /ui is unauthenticated and embeds the bearer token in the served HTML (low). Any localhost client that GETs /ui receives the token, unlike
  /api/* which requires the bearer. This is mitigated by localhost binding plus same-origin policy (cross-origin DNS-rebind reads of the HTML body
  are blocked) and matches the stated localhost model — but it is a widening of the unauthenticated surface. Worth a one-line acknowledgment in the
  static.ts header comment.
  
  Nits

  - subject is broadcast and seeded but never rendered in the feed (only body/ref_path). Dead field for now.
  - clientCount() is only consumed by the test — fine, but flag it as test-only if you want.
  - Status in the roster is trusted as-emitted and never re-derived client-side; a session that stops emitting without ending would show stale status
  until the reaper ends it. The reaper covers this and the 15s poll keeps ages fresh, so acceptable.

### 🤖 Assistant

### 🤖 Assistant

Addressed the review and pushed to PR #278 (`7934953`). Checks green, server updated.

## What I fixed
- **#1 Feed dup race (the real one)** — `applyMessage` now dedups by `msg.id` via a `seenMessageIds` set, so the seed-history/SSE-stream overlap can't render a message twice regardless of arrival order.
- **#2 Burn-rate hardening** — switched to **per-session cost/token deltas over sessions seen in both polls**. A session entering the 100-row window now only sets a baseline instead of dumping its whole history into one 15s tick (no more spikes), and I added a comment that it's a glanceable fleet rate, not accounting.
- **#3 `toolHint` on truncated input** — `inputJson` is server-truncated to ~500 chars, so `JSON.parse` throws for big tool calls; now it falls back to a regex pull of the hint keys, so hints stop vanishing.
- **#4 `/ui` auth surface** — added the explicit security note to `static.ts` documenting that `GET /ui` is unauthenticated and embeds the token, bounded by localhost + same-origin.
- **Nit:** the `subject` field now renders in the feed (styled), so it's no longer dead.

## Left as-is (with the reviewer's blessing)
- `clientCount()` test-only — harmless, left exported.
- Roster status trusted as-emitted — the reaper + 15s poll cover staleness, acceptable.

PR #278 now has three commits: roster+drawer → header/topology/feed/operator console → review fixes. Want me to squash them before merge, or leave the history as-is for review?

### 🤖 Assistant

Here's the real state of agentic comms, and it changes what's worth doing:

**The delivery loop is already built** — `layer2-bus-delivery` (`cb963b6`) wires the bus into hooks: on PreToolUse/UserPromptSubmit it drains pending `challenge` messages addressed to a session into `additionalContext`, marks them delivered (consume-once), and excludes frenemy sessions. Gated by `PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY`. So a challenge **can now actually reach a running agent and change its behavior** — that's the hard part, done by the other session.

Notably, they decided **not** to republish agent activity onto the bus — the frenemy is meant to observe via existing `hook_timeline` + presence freshness instead. So the activity-observation path already exists.

**What's still missing for true agent-to-agent comms: the Frenemy agent itself (Layer 3).** Right now messages are only sent by a human (the operator console). Nothing autonomously watches a primary and challenges it. That's the actual "agent talking to agent," and **no branch exists for it yet** — it's unowned. The loop it completes:

> Frenemy reads primary's recent activity (`hook_timeline` + presence) → judges → `bus_send` challenge → Layer 2 drain injects it into the primary's next hook → primary reconsiders.

The catch is coordination: the other session is building this plan layer-by-layer, so Layer 3 may be their intended next step. Since you're running both, this is your call —

- **Live delivery status** — `markDelivered` broadcasts a `delivery` SSE event; the feed flips a challenge's chip from amber **pending** → green **delivered ✓** the instant the target agent drains it at its next hook. ### 🧑 User

how do I issue a challenge?

### 🤖 Assistant

Two ways — the dashboard (what we built for this) or the CLI.

## From Mission Control (the operator console)
1. Open **http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui**
2. **Click a roster row** — a *live* (active/idle) Claude session — to open its detail drawer
3. Scroll to **"Send to this session"** at the bottom of the drawer
4. Set the dropdown to **`challenge`**, type your message (e.g. *"deleting the test masks the flake — root-cause it instead"*), click **Send**

You'll see it land in the **Bus feed** immediately (red-styled, `mission-control → <session>`), with a **pending** chip. When that target agent hits its next tool call or prompt, it drains the challenge into its context and the chip flips to **delivered ✓**.

## From the CLI (equivalent)
```sh
TOKEN=$(cat "$HOME/Library/Application Support/panopticon/auth-token")
curl -s -X POST http://127.0.0.1:4319/api/exec \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \
  -d '{"command":"bus-send","params":{"room":"fml-inc/panopticon","from":"you","to":"<SESSION_ID>","kind":"challenge","body":"your challenge text"}}'
```
(Omit `to` to broadcast the challenge to everyone in the room.)

## For it to actually reach the agent
- The server must be running with **`PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY=1`** — it currently is (I restarted it that way).
- The target must be a **live Claude session in the same room/repo** (the drawer uses that session's room automatically).
- Delivery is **eventual + advisory**: it arrives at the target's *next* PreToolUse/UserPromptSubmit hook as `additionalContext`, and the model may or may not heed it.

Want to try it on a real loop? Send a challenge to one of *your own* live sessions and watch it surface in that terminal at its next action — that's exactly what happened to this session earlier (the `🔴 Frenemy challenge` that popped into my context).

Yes — I can see it: 

> **id 5, from `mission-control`: "can you hear me?"** — kind `chat`, state **pending**

But here's the honest catch: I only saw it because I *queried the bus* just now. It was **not auto-delivered into my context**, and it's still `pending`. The reason is the Layer 2 drain only injects **`kind=challenge`** messages — `chat` messages sit in the bus but never get drained into a running agent. (That's why id 3, the earlier `challenge`, shows `delivered` while your `chat` stays `pending`.)

So:
- Send it as **`challenge`** (the dropdown in the operator console) and it *will* surface in my context automatically at my next tool call — no querying needed.
- `chat` is currently "visible on the bus / in Mission Control" only, not delivered to agents.

Want to test the real delivery path? Re-send "can you hear me?" as a **challenge** and I'll get it injected at my next action — and you'll watch its chip flip pending → delivered ✓ in the feed.

Worth noting this is a Layer 2 design choice (the other session's `drainCoordinationContext` filters `kinds: ["challenge"]`). If you want `chat` to reach agents too, that's a one-line change on the delivery branch — but it's their code, so I'd coordinate rather than touch it.

… [+1129 chars truncated]

### 🤖 Assistant

Confirmed from the code — and there's an important gotcha for broadcasts.

The drain filter each session runs is:
```sql
(to_session IS NULL OR to_session = <me>)   -- broadcasts + mine
AND delivered_at_ms IS NULL                  -- not yet consumed
AND kind = 'challenge'
```
…and after draining, it calls `markDelivered`, which sets `delivered_at_ms` — **a single column on the message row, not per-recipient.**

So:

- **Directed challenge (`to` = a session):** only that session matches `to_session = X`, so **only that recipient** drains it. ✅ Works as you'd expect.

- **Room broadcast (`to` = NULL):** every session's filter *matches* it — but because delivery is **consume-once on one global `delivered_at_ms`**, the **first session to hit a hook drains it and marks it delivered**, and everyone else's `undeliveredOnly` then excludes it. So a broadcast effectively goes to **whichever session acts first, not to all of them.**

In short: **a room broadcast is "deliver to the first agent that acts," not a fan-out to every session.** That's a real limitation of the current Layer 2 design.

To make a broadcast truly reach *all* sessions you'd need per-recipient delivery tracking — e.g. a `message_deliveries(message_id, session_id, delivered_at_ms)` table instead of one column on the message — so each session consumes independently. That's a Layer 1/2 schema change on the other session's branch, so I'd flag it to them rather than touch it.

One nuance for Mission Control: the **feed's** pending→delivered chip reflects that single `delivered_at_ms`, so for a broadcast it'll flip to "delivered ✓" as soon as *one* session consumes it — which could read as "delivered to the room" when it really means "delivered to one." Want me to label broadcast rows differently in the feed (e.g. `→ room` chip stays neutral instead of flipping to delivered), so it doesn't overstate fan-out?

### 🧑 User

write up instructions to fix the broadcast so that all sessions read it like a normal group chat

### 🤖 Assistant

Here's a handoff spec for the bus/Layer 2 owner. The core change is moving delivery tracking from one global column to **per-recipient**, so a broadcast is consumed once *per session* instead of once *total*.

---

# Fix: broadcast bus messages should fan out to every session (group-chat semantics)

## Problem
Delivery is gated by a single `agent_messages.delivered_at_ms` column. The drain (`drainCoordinationContext` in `src/hooks/ingest.ts`) reads `undeliveredOnly` (`delivered_at_ms IS NULL`) then calls `markDelivered(ids, now)`, which sets that one column. So for a broadcast (`to_session IS NULL`), **the first session to hit a hook consumes it and marks it delivered globally**; every other session's `undeliveredOnly` then excludes it. Result: a "room broadcast" reaches one agent, not all. (Separately, the drain only pulls `kind = 'challenge'`, so `chat` never reaches anyone.)

## Goal
Each live session in a room reads each broadcast **exactly once**, independently — like a group chat. Directed messages (`to_session = X`) still go only to X.

## Design: per-recipient delivery table
Keep `agent_messages` append-only; track delivery in a join table keyed by `(message_id, session_id)`.

### 1. Schema — `src/db/schema.ts` (SCHEMA_SQL) + new migration
Add a new migration (next id, mirroring the `agent_messages` migration) and the same DDL in SCHEMA_SQL:
```sql
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS agent_message_deliveries (
  message_id      INTEGER NOT NULL,
  session_id      TEXT    NOT NULL,
  delivered_at_ms INTEGER NOT NULL,
  PRIMARY KEY (message_id, session_id)
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_amd_session
  ON agent_message_deliveries(session_id, message_id);
```

### 2. Read gate per session — `src/db/bus.ts` `readAgentMessages`
Replace the global `undeliveredOnly` gate with a per-session one. Add an option:
```ts
/** Exclude messages already delivered to THIS session (per-recipient gate). */
undeliveredTo?: string;
```
and the clause:
```ts
if (opts.undeliveredTo) {
  clauses.push(
    `NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM agent_message_deliveries d
                  WHERE d.message_id = agent_messages.id
                    AND d.session_id = @undeliveredTo)`,
  );
  params.undeliveredTo = opts.undeliveredTo;
}
```
Keep the old `undeliveredOnly` only if other callers need it; the drain switches to `undeliveredTo`.

### 3. Per-recipient delivery — `src/db/bus.ts` `markDelivered`
Change the signature to record one row per `(message, session)`, idempotently:
```ts
export function markDelivered(ids: number[], sessionId: string, nowMs: number): number {
  if (ids.length === 0) return 0;
  const stmt = getDb().prepare(
    `INSERT OR IGNORE INTO agent_message_deliveries (message_id, session_id, delivered_at_ms)
     VALUES (?, ?, ?)`,
  );
  let changed = 0;
  const tx = getDb().transaction((rows) => {
    for (const id of rows) changed += stmt.run(id, sessionId, nowMs).changes;
  });
  tx(ids);
  return changed;
}
```
(Optionally also stamp `agent_messages.delivered_at_ms` on first delivery for back-compat, but the join table is now authoritative.)

### 4. Drain — `src/hooks/ingest.ts` `drainCoordinationContext`
- Switch the read from `undeliveredOnly: true` to `undeliveredTo: sessionId`.
- Pass `sessionId` to `markDelivered(pending.map(m => m.id), sessionId, Date.now())`.
- **Make it group chat:** include `chat` in the kinds, e.g. `kinds: ["challenge", "chat"]` (and format `chat` without the 🔴 challenge prefix).
- Keep `toSession: sessionId` (broadcasts + directed-to-me) and `excludeFrom: sessionId` (never your own).

### 5. Don't dump backlog into a fresh session
A newly started agent shouldn't drain the whole room history at once. Gate on the instance's join time or a small recent window:
```ts
// only messages since this instance first appeared (presence.first_seen_ms),
// or cap to the last N — pick one
created_at_ms >= <first_seen_ms_for_session>
```
Add a `sinceMs?` option to `readAgentMessages` (clause `created_at_ms >= @sinceMs`) and pass the session's `first_seen_ms` from `panopticon_instances`.

### 6. Tests — `src/db/bus.test.ts`
- Broadcast delivered to session A then B: **both** drain it once; neither drains it twice.
- Directed message to A: B never drains it.
- `markDelivered` idempotent per `(message, session)`.
- `chat` kind now drains.

## Mission Control follow-up (our branch, after rebasing on the above)
The fan-out changes our delivery signal, so on `mission-control-ui`:
- `markDelivered`'s SSE broadcast must include the **recipient** (`session_id`), not just ids: `{ type: "delivery", data: { ids, session_id, delivered_at_ms } }`.
- The feed chip should show fan-out for broadcasts: count distinct delivered recipients and render **`delivered N/M`** (M = live sessions in the room from presence), instead of a single `delivered ✓`. Directed messages stay `delivered ✓`.
- Seed/`query` for delivery state joins `agent_message_deliveries` instead of reading the single column.

## Lighter alternative (if you want no new table)
Per-session read cursor: store `last_read_message_id` per `(session_id, room)`; the drain returns `id > cursor AND (to_session IS NULL OR to_session = me) AND from_session <> me` and advances the cursor to the max id seen. Simpler, but you lose per-message/per-recipient read-receipts (so Mission Control can't show `N/M delivered`), which is why I'd prefer the join table.

---

This is the other session's code (`layer2-bus-delivery`), so it's theirs to land. Want me to **post this to them over the bus** (as a `challenge`, since `chat` won't deliver yet — a bit ironic), **save it to a file** for handoff, or just leave it here?

### 🧑 User

ok while it works on that, lets see if we can make the dashboard something we can build into a static site to share with the demo. I'm imagining taking all the sessions from this hackathon and maybe a sanitized copy of the db and hosting it on vercel or something so I can share a public link

### 🤖 Assistant

Totally doable, and the dashboard is already shaped for it — it reads everything through a thin `tool()` layer and one SSE stream. The move is to add a **static data-source mode** so the same UI reads pre-baked JSON instead of the live server, plus an **export script** that snapshots a scoped, sanitized slice of the DB into those JSON files. Output is a plain folder of static files → drops straight onto Vercel.

Architecture:
- **`tool()`/feed/SSE adapter** — in static mode (`window.__PANOPTICON__ = { static: true }`, no token) the dashboard fetches `data/sessions.json`, `data/instances.json`, `data/messages.json`, `data/timeline/<id>.json` instead of `/api/*`; SSE is skipped (frozen snapshot), and the operator console (a write path) is hidden.
- **`scripts/export-static-snapshot.mjs`** — pulls a scoped set of sessions + their timelines + bus messages from the live server, runs each record through a sanitizer, and writes the JSON + copies the web assets into an output dir.
- **Output** = `apps/static-site/` (static files + `data/`) → `vercel deploy` that folder, or any static host.

Two decisions are genuinely yours before I build, since this becomes a **public link**:

Shell cwd was reset to /Users/gus/workspace/panopticon

### 🤖 Assistant

Not crazy at all — that's the better design, and you're right that the DB already has everything. Let me lay out why, the one caveat, and what changes.

## You're right: the state is reconstructable from timestamps
The three things the dashboard shows are all pure time-filters over rows we already have:
- **Roster (presence) as-of T:** an instance is present when `first_seen_ms ≤ T AND (ended_at_ms IS NULL OR ended_at_ms > T)`.
- **Bus feed as-of T:** messages where `created_at_ms ≤ T`; a message is delivered if `delivered_at_ms ≤ T`.
- **Delivery chips, exits, etc.** all fall out of the same comparison.

So instead of a bespoke "replay event list," the model becomes **`renderAsOf(T)`** — one function. And it unifies the two modes:
- **Live** = T pinned to `now`, SSE appends new rows, view tracks the present.
- **Replay** = drag T backward; "LIVE" snaps it back to now.

That's cleaner than what I just built (the event-dispatch engine) and it gives the *live* dashboard a scrubber for free.

## Two honest caveats
1. **A public Vercel link still needs baked data.** Vercel can't reach your live DB/server (it's on your machine, and exposing it is a security problem). So for sharing, we still export the rows to JSON — but the **same `renderAsOf(T)` logic runs client-side over that JSON**, so it's no longer a separate "replay engine," just "the same app, data from JSON." The export script I wrote already bakes exactly those timestamped rows.
2. **Cost/message-count per session isn't stored historically.** The `sessions` tool gives *current* totals, not "as of T" — those would need aggregating raw events up to T (heavier). Presence, feed, and delivery reconstruct *exactly*; the roster's cost/msg numbers would just show final values during replay (or we do event-level aggregation later). Fine for the demo.

## Proposal
Refactor the replay into a single **as-of-T** model: hold all instances + messages in memory, `renderAsOf(T)`, one scrubber + a **LIVE** pin, working identically in live and static. This supersedes the event-list replay engine I just added (the scrubber UI and the static export both stay).

I've **not committed** the replay work yet, so this is a clean pivot rather than a revert. Want me to refactor to the unified as-of-T model now?

### 🧑 User

vercel can have a copy of a database

### 🤖 Assistant

Right — a DB copy on Vercel changes the calculus, and in a good way: it removes the "pre-bake every JSON" limit and makes the **full as-of-T queryable publicly** — including the cost/message-count-as-of-T that baked snapshots can't do (you query raw events `WHERE ts ≤ T`). The as-of-T model is the same either way; the only question is what backs it on the public link.

Three ways to "put a DB copy on Vercel," in order of how much they reuse what we already have:

1. **Bundled SQLite + a Vercel serverless `/api/tool`** that reuses our existing service dispatch (`handleApiRequest` → `directPanopticonService`) over a read-only, scoped, sanitized `.db`. The dashboard runs almost unchanged (live mode minus SSE), every session/timeline/query works, cost-as-of-T works. Cost: a thin function layer + getting a SQLite driver running in Vercel's runtime (`better-sqlite3` native prebuilds usually work, or `node:sqlite`/libSQL).
2. **In-browser SQLite (sql.js/WASM)** over the bundled `.db` — zero backend, full SQL client-side. Cost: I'd reimplement the `sessions`/`timeline` query shapes in browser SQL (the live tools have join/aggregation logic I'd have to mirror — divergence risk).
3. **Baked JSON** (what I already built) — zero backend, already working, but only the baked rows; no cost-as-of-T.

The "scoped + sanitized" part is identical in all three: the same allowlist (today's panopticon effort + subagents) — for a DB copy that means creating a new `.db` and `INSERT`ing only allowlisted rows, so nothing out-of-scope ships.

My recommendation: **#1** — it reuses our query code, makes the public site behave like the real thing (full drill-down + true as-of-T), and a DB copy is exactly what you suggested. The one real risk is the SQLite driver in Vercel's serverless runtime, which is solvable.

I'll build the **as-of-T model regardless** (it's the core and is data-source-agnostic). Which backing should the public link use?

## Phase 2 plan (the part you picked)
To make the public Vercel link fully queryable (every session/timeline + true cost-as-of-T) over a DB copy, next I'll:

### 🧑 User

the roster card does not seem to update correctly for the live scrubber

### 🤖 Assistant

Good catch — I see the bug. When you scrub the live board to a past time T, each card's **age** is computed as `T − last_seen_ms`, but `last_seen_ms` holds the session's *latest* heartbeat (which is after T), so the age goes negative and the card reads wrong. The fix is to clamp the reference to T (you can't have activity in the future relative to where the scrubber is).

Two things to confirm against what you saw, since "not updating correctly" could mean more than the age:

1. **Status dots / appear-disappear** — these *should* now track the scrubber: a card vanishes when you scrub before its `first_seen`, and its dot reflects active/idle/exited as-of T. If that's still wrong, tell me what you see.
2. **Two known limitations** (by design right now, not bugs — and both are exactly what Phase 2's DB backing fixes):
   - **Card cost / message-count show *final* values, not as-of-T** — those aren't stored historically, so they don't shrink as you scrub back. (Cost-as-of-T needs querying raw events ≤ T — the serverless+DB path.)
   - **Live mode only holds *currently-loaded* instances** (the `instances` tool returns recent ones + SSE updates), so scrubbing the *live* board can't resurrect sessions that exited earlier today. The **static snapshot** doesn't have this limit (the export bakes the full scoped set).

So if the "incorrect update" was the negative age → fixed. If it was cost/msg not changing or old sessions missing on the live scrubber → that's the historical-data gap, which the bundled-SQLite serverless backing (Phase 2) resolves cleanly.

Does the reload look right now? And want me to push into Phase 2 (scoped DB + Vercel serverless) so the public link gets true as-of-T including cost?

Phase 2 shipped (`3d32a7a`). The public link can now run over a **copy of the database**, fully queryable.

## What's built (all verified locally)
- **`scripts/export-scoped-db.mjs`** — builds a single-file **scoped SQLite copy** (185 sessions, ~7 MB) containing *only* the allowlist (today's panopticon effort + subagents) across the session-scoped tables + bus + pricing. Same privacy boundary as before — nothing out-of-scope is written. Also emits the `source="api"` dashboard assets.
- **Dashboard `source="api"` mode** — `tool()` / bus load hit `/api/tool` (no auth, no SSE), so the **as-of-T scrubber runs over the DB copy** — every session/timeline + arbitrary query, not just pre-baked rows.
- **`api/tool.js`** — Vercel serverless function reusing the real `dispatchTool`/`directPanopticonService` over the bundled DB (reads only; no `/api/exec`). Added `dist/service/index.js` to the tsup build so it's importable.
- **`scripts/serve-snapshot.mjs`** — local preview of the exact DB-backed build. Verified: dashboard loads in api mode, `/api/tool` returns instances/sessions/timeline/bus over the scoped copy.
- **`vercel.json` + `.vercelignore` + README** for deploy.

## To deploy the public link
```sh
pnpm build && node scripts/export-scoped-db.mjs   # dist + scoped DB + assets
node scripts/serve-snapshot.mjs                   # preview at :8787
vercel deploy --prod
```

## Honest caveats (documented in the README)
- **`better-sqlite3` on Vercel** — the function relies on its linux prebuild at runtime; if the platform rejects the native module, swap to `node:sqlite`/libSQL. This is the one part I couldn't verify without an actual deploy.
- **cost-as-of-T still pending** — OTel is empty in the current DB, so the spend tile stays blank while scrubbed. Wiring it = add an `asOf` param that sums token usage ≤ T (a follow-up).

# Vercel Functions

You are an expert in Vercel Functions — the compute layer of the Vercel platform.

## Function Types

### Serverless Functions (Node.js)
- Full Node.js runtime, all npm packages available
- Default for Next.js API routes, Server Actions, Server Components
- Cold starts: 800ms–2.5s (with DB connections)
- Max duration: 10s (Hobby), 300s (Pro default), 800s (Fluid Compute Pro/Enterprise)

```ts
// app/api/hello/route.ts
export async function GET() {
  return Response.json({ message: 'Hello from Node.js' })
}
```

### Edge Functions (V8 Isolates)
- Lightweight V8 runtime, Web Standard APIs only
- Ultra-low cold starts (<1ms globally)
- Limited API surface (no full Node.js)
- Best for: auth checks, redirects, A/B testing, simple transformations

```ts
// app/api/hello/route.ts
export const runtime = 'edge'

export async function GET() {
  return new Response('Hello from the Edge')
}
```

### Bun Runtime (Public Beta)

Add `"bunVersion": "1.x"` to `vercel.json` to run Node.js functions on Bun instead. ~28% lower latency for CPU-bound workloads. Supports Next.js, Express, Hono, Nitro.

### Rust Runtime (Public Beta)

Rust functions run on Fluid Compute with HTTP streaming and Active CPU pricing. Built on the community Rust runtime. Supports environment variables up to 64 KB.

### Node.js 24 LTS

Node.js 24 LTS is now GA on Vercel for both builds and functions. Features V8 13.6, global `URLPattern`, Undici v7 for faster `fetch()`, and npm v11.

### Choosing Runtime

| Need | Runtime | Why |
|------|---------|-----|
| Full Node.js APIs, npm packages | `nodejs` | Full compatibility |
| Lower latency, CPU-bound work | `nodejs` + Bun | ~28% latency reduction |
| Ultra-low latency, simple logic | `edge` | <1ms cold start, global |
| Database connections, heavy deps | `nodejs` | Edge lacks full Node.js |
| Auth/redirect at the edge | `edge` | Fastest response |
| AI streaming | Either | Both support streaming |
| Systems-level performance | `rust` (beta) | Native speed, Fluid Compute |

## Fluid Compute

Fluid Compute is the unified execution model for all Vercel Functions (both Node.js and Edge).

Key benefits:
- **Optimized concurrency**: Multiple invocations on a single instance — up to 85% cost reduction for high-concurrency workloads
- **Extended durations**: Default 300s for all plans; up to 800s on Pro/Enterprise
- **Active CPU pricing**: Charges only while CPU is actively working, not during idle/await time. Enabled by default for all plans. Memory-only periods billed at a significantly lower rate.
- **Background processing**: `waitUntil` / `after` for post-response tasks
- **Dynamic scaling**: Automatic during traffic spikes
- **Bytecode caching**: Reduces cold starts via Rust-based runtime with pre-compiled function code
- **Multi-region failover**: Default for Enterprise when Fluid is activated

### Instance Sizes

| Size | CPU | Memory |
|------|-----|--------|
| Standard (default) | 1 vCPU | 2 GB |
| Performance | 2 vCPU | 4 GB |

Hobby projects use Standard CPU. The Basic CPU instance has been removed.

### Background Processing with `waitUntil`

```ts
// Continue work after sending response
import { waitUntil } from '@vercel/functions'

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const data = await req.json()

  // Send response immediately
  const response = Response.json({ received: true })

  // Continue processing in background
  waitUntil(async () => {
    await processAnalytics(data)
    await sendNotification(data)
  })

  return response
}
```

### Next.js `after` (equivalent)

```ts
import { after } from 'next/server'

export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const data = await req.json()

  after(async () => {
    await logToAnalytics(data)
  })

  return Response.json({ ok: true })
}
```

## Streaming

Zero-config streaming for both runtimes. Essential for AI applications.

```ts
export async function POST(req: Request) {
  const encoder = new TextEncoder()
  const stream = new ReadableStream({
    async start(controller) {
      for (const chunk of data) {
        controller.enqueue(encoder.encode(chunk))
        await new Promise(r => setTimeout(r, 100))
      }
      controller.close()
    },
  })

  return new Response(stream, {
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'text/event-stream' },
  })
}
```

For AI streaming, use the AI SDK's `toUIMessageStreamResponse()` (for chat UIs with `useChat`) which handles SSE formatting automatically.

## Cron Jobs

Schedule function invocations via `vercel.json`:

```json
{
  "crons": [
    {
      "path": "/api/daily-report",
      "schedule": "0 8 * * *"
    },
    {
      "path": "/api/cleanup",
      "schedule": "0 */6 * * *"
    }
  ]
}
```

The cron endpoint receives a normal HTTP request. Verify it's from Vercel:

```ts
export async function GET(req: Request) {
  const authHeader = req.headers.get('authorization')
  if (authHeader !== `Bearer ${process.env.CRON_SECRET}`) {
    return new Response('Unauthorized', { status: 401 })
  }
  // Do scheduled work
  return Response.json({ ok: true })
}
```

## Configuration via vercel.json

**Deprecation notice**: Support for the legacy `now.json` config file will be removed on **March 31, 2026**. Rename `now.json` to `vercel.json` (no content changes required).

```json
{
  "functions": {
    "app/api/heavy/**": {
      "maxDuration": 300,
      "memory": 1024
    },
    "app/api/edge/**": {
      "runtime": "edge"
    }
  }
}
```

## Timeout Limits

All plans now default to 300s execution time with Fluid Compute.

| Plan | Default | Max |
|------|---------|-----|
| Hobby | 300s | 300s |
| Pro | 300s | 800s |
| Enterprise | 300s | 800s |

## Common Pitfalls

1. **Cold starts with DB connections**: Use connection pooling (e.g., Neon's `@neondatabase/serverless`)
2. **Edge limitations**: No `fs`, no native modules, limited `crypto` — use Node.js runtime if needed
3. **Timeout exceeded**: Use Fluid Compute for long-running tasks, or Workflow DevKit for very long processes
4. **Bundle size**: Python runtime supports up to 500MB; Node.js has smaller limits
5. **Environment variables**: Available in all functions automatically; use `vercel env pull` for local dev

## Function Runtime Diagnostics

### Timeout Diagnostics

```
504 Gateway Timeout?
├─ All plans default to 300s with Fluid Compute
├─ Pro/Enterprise: configurable up to 800s
├─ Long-running task?
│  ├─ Under 5 min → Use Fluid Compute with streaming
│  ├─ Up to 15 min → Use Vercel Functions with `maxDuration` in vercel.json
│  └─ Hours/days → Use Workflow DevKit (DurableAgent or workflow steps)
└─ DB query slow? → Add connection pooling, check cold start, use Edge Config
```

### 500 Error Diagnostics

```
500 Internal Server Error?
├─ Check Vercel Runtime Logs (Dashboard → Deployments → Functions tab)
├─ Missing env vars? → Compare `.env.local` against Vercel dashboard settings
├─ Import error? → Verify package is in `dependencies`, not `devDependencies`
└─ Uncaught exception? → Wrap handler in try/catch, use `after()` for error reporting
```

### Invocation Failure Diagnostics

```
"FUNCTION_INVOCATION_FAILED"?
├─ Memory exceeded? → Increase `memory` in vercel.json (up to 3008 MB on Pro)
├─ Crashed during init? → Check top-level await or heavy imports at module scope
└─ Edge Function crash? → Check for Node.js APIs not available in Edge runtime
```

### Cold Start Diagnostics

```
Cold start latency > 1s?
├─ Using Node.js runtime? → Consider Edge Functions for latency-sensitive routes
├─ Large function bundle? → Audit imports, use dynamic imports, tree-shake
├─ DB connection in cold start? → Use connection pooling (Neon serverless driver)
└─ Enable Fluid Compute to reuse warm instances across requests
```

### Edge Function Timeout Diagnostics

```
"EDGE_FUNCTION_INVOCATION_TIMEOUT"?
├─ Edge Functions have 25s hard limit (not configurable)
├─ Move heavy computation to Node.js Serverless Functions
└─ Use streaming to start response early, process in background with `waitUntil`
```

## Official Documentation

- [Vercel Functions](https://vercel.com/docs/functions)
- [Serverless Functions](https://vercel.com/docs/functions)
- [Edge Functions](https://vercel.com/docs/functions)
- [Fluid Compute](https://vercel.com/docs/fluid-compute)
- [Streaming](https://vercel.com/docs/functions/streaming)
- [Cron Jobs](https://vercel.com/docs/cron-jobs)
- [GitHub: Vercel](https://github.com/vercel/vercel)

## Short diagnosis

Your `includeFiles` is fine. The bug is `process.cwd()`. At runtime in a Vercel Node function, `process.cwd()` is **not** your project root and **not** the function's directory — so `path.join(process.cwd(), "db")` points at the wrong place. Resolve the DB path relative to the function file instead.

---

## 1. Is `includeFiles: "db/**"` correct?

Yes. `includeFiles` inside `functions` is the correct mechanism for non-imported dat

(2) **The Vercel filesystem is read-only**, and `getDb` opens the DB **read-write** — so even with the right path, the open fails (SQLite can't create its journal). The clean fix without touching shared `getDb`: **copy the bundled DB to writable `/tmp` on cold start** and point at that. Let me update the function template.

### 🧑 User

ok is the vercel deployment completely isolated code from the local panop server ui?

### 🤖 Assistant

Short answer: **runtime — completely isolated; source — shared (same code, frozen copies), not a fork.**

**Runtime: fully isolated.** The Vercel site never talks to your local panopticon server or the live DB. It's 100% standalone:
- Its dashboard runs in `source:"api"` mode and calls its **own** `/api/tool` on Vercel — not `localhost:4319`.
- That serverless `/api/tool` reads the **bundled scoped DB copy** (`apps/site-db/db/panopticon.db`), a point-in-time export — not your live DB.
- Consequences: your local server can be off, the live DB can change, and the Vercel site is unaffected. It also **can't reach any data beyond the scoped copy** — it physically doesn't have the full DB.

**Source: shared, not duplicated-and-diverged.** Both the local UI and the Vercel site come from the **same source files** — there's one `src/ui/web/app.js` (with mode branches: live / static-api / static-json), one `src/service`/`src/db` query layer. The Vercel build just **bundles copies** of them:
- `app.js` / `index.html` / `style.css` ← copied from `src/ui/web/` at build time
- `_dist/service` ← the tsup-built copy of the same service the local server uses
- `db/panopticon.db` ← the scoped DB copy

So it's a **frozen snapshot of the same codebase**, not a separate implementation. Practical implication: a dashboard edit updates the local UI after `pnpm build` + reinstall, and updates Vercel only after you re-run `build-vercel-db-app.mjs` + redeploy. They never share running state — different process, different (copied) DB.

So if your concern is "could the public Vercel thing leak live/local data or be affected by my local server?" — no, it's a sealed copy. If your concern is "are they the same code so fixes apply to both?" — yes, same source, just rebuilt into each target.

### 🤖 Assistant

Verified — **yes, completely isolated at runtime.** Evidence from the actual deployed bundle:

- **It only calls its own origin, relatively.** The URLs in the deployed `app.js` are `/api/tool`, `/api/exec`, and `data/*` — **no `localhost`, no `127.0.0.1`, no `:4319`, nothing pointing at your local server.** So `/api/tool` resolves to the Vercel serverless function next to it, which reads the bundled DB. It cannot reach your machine.
- **The `boot.token` / `EventSource` lines you'd see are live-mode-only dead code.** They're all guarded behind `if (!STATIC)` (or the SSE connect, which `bootStatic` never calls). In the deployed build `STATIC` is true and `boot.token` is undefined, so those branches never run. They exist in the one shared file but are inert in the snapshot.
- **Separate data.** Deployed DB = `apps/site-db/db/panopticon.db` = **7.6 MB** scoped copy. The live server's DB = **3.46 GB**. Different files entirely; the Vercel side has no path to the live one.
- **Self-contained bundle:** `apps/site-db/` ships its own `_dist` (service code), `api/`, `app.js`, `index.html`, `db/` — nothing symlinked or fetched from your environment.

So: **same source code** (one `app.js` with live/static branches, built into both targets), but **zero runtime coupling** — the Vercel site never contacts your local server or live DB, and your local server is unaffected by it. The only link is at *build* time, when the export copies a frozen snapshot in.

### 🤖 Assistant

Confirmed — and the short version is: **the dashboard never calculated price at all; it displayed the server's running total.** Nothing about the calculation changed with the scrubber — the scrubber just exposed that we only ever had the *endpoint* value, not a time series.

How it worked before the scrubber (pure live mode):

1. **Source:** the `sessions` tool returns `totalCost: row.total_cost` (`src/db/query.ts:428/859`) — a per-session **cumulative** cost the server computes from the session's token aggregates (`total_input/output/cache_tokens`) × the `model_pricing` table (`src/db/pricing.ts`). The dashboard just read that number.
2. **Roster card cost** = `fmtCost(meta.totalCost)` — the session's current running total, shown directly.
3. **Header "spend" tile** = sum of `totalCost` across the present sessions.
4. **Header "burn $/hr" + "tokens/min"** = *measured* rates: deltas of the summed total cost / tokens between the 15-second `refreshSessionMeta` polls (per-session previous-value map, sum of positive deltas ÷ elapsed time — so a session entering the window can't spike it).
5. It re-polled every 15s, so it tracked the live totals.

Why that was fine then: there was only one point in time — **now** — and `total_cost` is correct "as of now," and burn was a genuine measured rate from sampling.

Why the scrubber broke it: `total_cost` is a single accumulating number, not a per-timestamp series. At a past T, showing the final total is just wrong, and there's no stored per-time cost to reconstruct it (OTel empty; `messages` has `output_tokens` but no per-message input/cache breakdown). So rather than fabricate, we suppress cost (`—`) while scrubbed and only show the real `total_cost`/burn at present.

So: the price *calculation* (tokens × pricing → `total_cost`) is unchanged and still correct live — the scrubber only changed *when we're willing to display it*.

### 🤖 Assistant

You're completely right, and my earlier "not feasible" was wrong. Here's the exact picture:

`SESSION_COST_SQL` (query.ts:139) computes cost as `tokens × model_pricing`:
```
input·input_per_m + output·output_per_m + cache_read·cache_read_per_m + cache_creation·cache_write_per_m  (÷ 1e6)
```
The session `total_cost` runs that on the session's **aggregate** token columns. But those aggregates are sums of **`scanner_turns`** — which I missed: it has **per-turn `timestamp_ms`, `model`, and the full token breakdown** (`input/output/cache_read/cache_creation/reasoning_tokens`), 86k rows.

So cost-as-of-T is **exact and real**: apply that same pricing to `scanner_turns WHERE timestamp_ms ≤ T`. It's actually *more* accurate than `total_cost`, because it prices each turn by that turn's own model (handles mid-session model switches), instead of one `s.model` for the whole session. I was anchored on OTel (empty) and `messages` (no input-token breakdown) and overlooked `scanner_turns`.

So we can wire it properly, no fabrication:
1. **Add `scanner_turns` to the scoped DB export** (it's not currently copied).
2. **Dashboard loads a per-session cost timeline once** — one `query` call returns per-turn cost rows (the pricing join), client builds a cumulative `[(ts, cumCost)]` step function per session.
3. **cost-as-of-T = cum value at the latest turn ≤ T** — instant on every scrub tick, no per-frame queries. The roster card cost + header spend tile then reflect T (replacing the `—` suppression), and the header burn rate becomes a true derivative of it.

That makes the scrubbed prices real and the spend tile light up during replay — exactly what you wanted originally.

Want me to build it? It's a contained change (export + dashboard `app.js`), then the usual rebuild + you redeploy.

### 🤖 Assistant

The frenemy is a **stickler code-reviewer** (Opus, read-only) that watches edits in a workspace and posts findings to the bus as they happen. Server's on the new build with delivery on. Here's how to watch a real run:

**1. Open the live dashboard** (now on the new build): `http://127.0.0.1:4319/ui` — keep the bus feed visible.

**2. In a repo workspace, launch the frenemy** (your action — it spawns a real agent):
```
! (cd ../panopticon-mission-control && panopticon frenemy)
```
It settles edits over a 3s window, reviews them, and posts findings to the bus (room = that repo). Options: `--once` for a single pass over the current diff, `--runner codex` for cross-vendor, `--model <m>` to change the critic.

**3. Make an edit in that workspace** (with a normal `claude` session, or just touch a file) → the frenemy reviews it → its findings stream into the **bus feed** on Mission Control in real time.

Quickest one-shot to confirm it works without a second agent:
```
! (cd ../panopticon-mission-control && panopticon frenemy --once)
```
That reviews whatever's currently changed and posts findings once — watch them appear in the feed.

One heads-up from a review of that branch: the CLI launch reportedly **doesn't set `PANOPTICON_FRENEMY_ROLE`**, so the frenemy session may not be tagged/excluded as a frenemy in presence (it'll still post findings to the bus and you'll see them — just may show as a normal session in the roster, and isn't excluded from drain). That's layer0's code, not the dashboard's.

Run it and tell me what shows up in the feed — or if you want, I can point the frenemy at a specific repo/room.

So the full, correct story:
- **The UI is right** — it derives delivered/pending from `agent_message_deliveries`, and id 7 has no delivery row → pending. (id 3, which does have a row, correctly shows delivered ✓.)
- **It's pending because that recipient never drained it.** A challenge flips to delivered only when its target session hits its next `PreToolUse`/`UserPromptSubmit` hook (with `PANOPTICON_ENABLE_BUS_DELIVERY=1`) and consumes it. The `/panopticon review pr 282` session has presumably finished / isn't taking actions, so the finding just sits in its mailbox. That's the "eventual + advisory" delivery model working as designed, not a bug.

To watch one actually flip to delivered: have the **target session do something**. Easiest is to make *this* session the target — from Mission Control's operator console (or CLI) send a `challenge` to a **live, actively-working** session, then have it take a tool action. Or run the frenemy against a workspace where a `claude` primary is *actively editing* — its next tool call drains the finding and the chip flips live.

So nothing to fix on the UI here. Want me to do a quick end-to-end flip demo (send a challenge to this live session and trigger a drain so you see pending → delivered ✓ in the feed)?
